### Post by amjjawad on 2011-09-15
The information in this thread has been moved to [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/LubuntuLinks](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/LubuntuLinks)

A thread for discussion of the wiki page only can be found here [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=12062200#post12062200](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=12062200#post12062200)


[B][COLOR="Sienna"][COLOR="RoyalBlue"]Edit bodhi.zazen:

The forums staff appreciates the dedication and hard work amjjawad has put into the Lubuntu One Stop Thread and recognizes that this thread is an invaluable resource to the Lubuntu community.

However, we now have a thread that has over 500 posts with nuggets of information scattered about it that are impossible to find, and thus does not meet up to [[COLOR="DarkRed"]forums standards for tutorials[/COLOR]](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=677396)

As per [[COLOR="DarkRed"]this thread[/COLOR]](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1949027), we would like to see the information on this thread relocated to the wiki. The advantages of the wiki are that it is Community maintained, peer reviewed, easier to maintain, and easier to find information as compared to a 500 + thread on the forums.

We have staff available to help with convert the information to the wiki, we have asked amjjawad for assistance, and we are also asking the lubuntu community to participate. The wiki is community maintained.

[[COLOR="DarkRed"]bodhi.zazen[/COLOR]](http://ubuntuforums.org/member.php?u=89054) has been working on a script to help convert forums posts -> wiki syntax. [[[COLOR="DarkRed"]link to script on wiki[/COLOR]](http://bodhizazen.net/tweaks/ubforums2ubwiki.sh.txt)]. [/COLOR][/COLOR][/B]

[b][[COLOR="DarkOrange"]nothingspecial[/COLOR]](http://ubuntuforums.org/member.php?u=491516) [COLOR="RoyalBlue"]has volunteered from the forums staff to assist the lubuntu community.

See also : [/color][[COLOR="Navy"]Lubuntu Documentation Team[/COLOR]](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu/DocumentationTeam)[/b]



[CENTER][LEFT][COLOR=Red]**Please, read this first**[/COLOR]: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=11443852&postcount=172](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=11443852&postcount=172)

[/LEFT]

[COLOR=Navy][SIZE=6]**LOST**[/SIZE][SIZE=4](Lubuntu One Stop Thread)[/SIZE][/COLOR]
[SIZE=2](Previously known as: Lubuntu 11.04 - HOWTOs/Guides)[/SIZE] 
[/CENTER]


[U][B][SIZE=5]Welcome:[/SIZE]
[/B][/U]Hello and Welcome to Lubuntu One Stop Thread, the best place to know more about Lubuntu. Hope you enjoy and find what you were looking for and if you didn't, that is not a problem at all.


[U][B][SIZE=5]Introduction:[/SIZE]
[/B][/U]I have started this thread with two HOWTOs/Guides for Lubuntu but day after day, I realized that Lubuntu Community specifically and Ubuntu Community generally need something beyond that. Thus, I have decided to make this thread as "One Stop Thread" for Lubuntu which means it will contain EVERYTHING about Lubuntu. I'll make sure to update it on daily basis.

As always, I'm waiting for any suggestions/feedback/question you may have so please, feel home.

Thank you so much for choosing and using Lubuntu. 
Because of **YOU**, Lubuntu has reached where it's right now and because of **YOU**, Lubuntu will continue dazzling everyone.

[B]P.S.
[/B]Any thing will be posted here (Guides/HOWTOs/Tutorials/etc) must be tested first to ensure it will work on everyone's machine. My Guides/HOWTOs will be tested before posting so please make sure yours are tested too.


[SIZE=5]**_HOWTO Use Lubuntu One Stop Thread?_**
[/SIZE]
Kindly STICK to this gentle reminder as long as you are here:

[IMG]http://i43.tinypic.com/zv22ow.jpg[/IMG]

**FOR MORE information, please read this:** [http://ubuntuforums.org/index.php?page=policy](http://ubuntuforums.org/index.php?page=policy)

Please have a look at [**[COLOR=Red]this simple and short guide[/COLOR]**]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=11443852&postcount=172").

Also, please have a look at: [SIZE=4][**How To Write an Informative and Detailed Thread**]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=11532952&postcount=349")[/SIZE]

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-10-17
**[SIZE=4][COLOR=Red]*[/COLOR][/SIZE]** [B][COLOR=DarkRed]
Please be informed that this section has been slightly changed. Now, this section will have ALL Lubuntu Threads on Ubuntu Forum. Solved or Unsolved. This will make it even easier and faster for anyone to search for a thread. Some UNSOLVED threads have valuable posts and information.[/COLOR][/B]


[B][SIZE=4][COLOR=Red]HOW TO USE THIS?
HOW TO SEARCH FOR A THREAD?[/COLOR]
[/SIZE][/B]

[LIST]
[*]Simply, use the search function on your browser. For example, **Ctrl+F** on Firefox or Chromium.
[*]Enter the Keyword you are looking for and Press Enter.
[*]If you couldn't find what are you looking for then please **[see this]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=11430493&postcount=140")**.
[*]Done :)
[/LIST]

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-10-26
> **Rodney9 said:**
> I thought the L in Lubuntu was for Love :mrgreen:

Why shouldn't it? I guess it's :)
It depends on who you see it or want it to be. Everything is possible in Linux, just set your mind free and dream bigger.


> My preferences are set the same but still a store bought pre-recorded music CD still wants to be opened in the file manager which it fails with a error or wants to be burnt with xfburn. Can't you set to auto play ? At least Audacious sees it and can play it.I honestly didn't get time to test that but I sure will do hopefully soon, I'm just having lots of issues here that I must deal with, sorry.

> Another question, is there a way to change the wallpaper every 30 mins or 5 or every hour ? I have tried Wally, DesktopNova, Wallch in Xubuntu and none work, I am hoping with Lubuntu it will be simple.
Windows Stuff, eh? :P
Well, don't know if any but I see you found one approach to do that :)

> Then one more question, if I may, I saw in one of your posts that you are using 11.04, why not 11.10 and do they look the same ?
Yes. I'm using 11.04 just because I don't need to use the new one :)
I've tested 11.10 and I know what are the differences that I came across myself so I don't really have to use it. However, I have it installed on 4GB USB Drive so in case someone asks about 11.10, I can use that to help him. Funny I don't have time to myself. My whole time is dedicated to Lubuntu and this forum so I'm having tests machines here for that purpose :)

The default system is newer and at some point with different options. For example, Power-Management package in 11.10 is xfce not gnome. Default look is different. More themes, 6 new wallpapers, etc.
Check the release notes :) it's on page one, I think section D?

 
> I am thinking of putting Lubuntu 11.10 64bit on my desktop as well, so I would be interested to hear your opinions on 11.04 and 11.10Both are great. I've been using Lubutnu since 10.04 and I can confirm there is a huge difference in everything. It's getting better after each release. I'm just happy with 11.04 and I see no point to use the new one. I'm using the new only for my tests, writing guides and helping others. I'm involved in testing, writing guides, wiki and forum support.

Go ahead and use the latest. However, sometimes, even the latest releases won't work perfectly well on your hardware so you may need to use an older but supported version. I have come across a case where the user have problem with all Ubuntu variant 11.10 while he has no issues with 11.04. Depends.

> Thank you for your help, you're top panel looks fantastic how did you do that, is it Cairo ?
You most welcome and thanks for your nice words.

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-10-27
[U][B][SIZE=4]Introduction[/SIZE]
[/B][/U]
There is an [known bug]("https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/casper/+bug/854837") which is unfortunately effecting many releases so far. However, I noticed with the final release (11.10) that his problem fade away once you use Live-USB.

Whether you'll face that problem or not, I'm going to write a simple and short guide to help everyone to avoid it and have some workaround to get to the Live-Desktop of Lubuntu and try it without installation.

[U][B][SIZE=4]Workaround[/SIZE]
[/B][/U]
1- Boot your machine from the Live-CD

2- On this screen, choose your language:

[IMG]http://i51.tinypic.com/30urd04.jpg[/IMG]




3- On this screen, the default option is "**Try Lubuntu without installation"**. Please skip to the second option which is [B][COLOR=Red]"Install Lubuntu"

[IMG]http://i53.tinypic.com/2cql5de.jpg[/IMG]
[/COLOR][/B]




4- After some time, you'll see a Desktop with only one screen

[IMG]http://i40.tinypic.com/2v28pyu.jpg[/IMG]


Please, click **[COLOR=Red]Quit[/COLOR]** then confirm with [COLOR=Red]**Quit**[/COLOR].

After that, you'll get the Live Desktop with the icon of Install Lubuntu.


5- After you finish your test and if everything will work for you, you can start the installation again:

[IMG]http://i41.tinypic.com/iqfr53.jpg[/IMG]



Enjoy :)

P.S.
[Release Notes]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu/ReleaseNotes/OneiricOcelot") = Updated
[Wiki Page]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Lubuntu/Documentation/FAQ/Workarounds") = Updated
[Installation Guide]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Lubuntu/InstallingLubuntu") = Updated

---

### Post by jontheid on 2011-10-28
Hi
I am running Lubuntu 11.10 on my 2nd laptop - a Toshiba Satellite l30-101 with a 1.4Ghz celeron and a whopping 431MB of RAM.
It runs really well, very snappy. Faster than Ubuntu/Xubuntu/XP any day.

I have compiz running smoothly, my printer is working, my wireless is working, my webcam is working, my scanner is working and I can access my other windows machines files.

I really like Lubuntu - I have tried quite a few different flavours of linux and this one seems to be the best on this laptop.

I think that this One Stop Thread is a great idea.

Can I make a few suggestions?

1) The link to the Lubuntu website on the first post on the thread is wrong - it links to [http://ubuntuforums.org/www.lubuntu.net](http://ubuntuforums.org/www.lubuntu.net)
when it should be just
[http://www.lubuntu.net](http://www.lubuntu.net)

2) Some of the 'solved thread' links are actually a bit hard to follow. The one on 'how to enable compositing' gets a bit confusing. 
Wouldn't it be better to rewrite these specifically as a 'how to' and link to that from the front page.

3) Would it be good to include 'how to' pages for general Linux things but with a lubuntu slant? 
Examples:

* access windows shared files. This drove me insane in Lubuntu as I could see the files in 'network drives' fine but nothing would open properly by clicking on it. Things changes radically once I had installed 'gigolo' to mount the smb directories

* install medibuntu packages so DVDs play etc

* install/build madwifi (something I need to do as ath5k just doesn't cut it with my wireless card)

* how to set up compiz - another thing that bent my brain.
Changing the window manager in 'desktop session settings' does absolutely nothing at all! Finally got it working by changing 
.config/lxsession/Lubuntu/desktop.conf


This is about the 15th time I have toyed with using Linux and it is about the first time I think I am going to stick with it, primarily because Lubuntu is so good. 

I think if we make it as easy as possible for the average computer user to set up their system with Lubuntu, with the ability to do all the things they can do in Windows, the better.

Btw one of the reasons I use compiz is to make the edges of the windows thicker so it isn't so fiddly to resize horizontally. With openbox the window edges are so thin you have to be almost pixel-perfect to grab the edge. Is there a simple work-around for this that doesn't require compiz?

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-10-29
> **Orographic said:**

Really enjoying the 11.10 version of Lubuntu. [COLOR=Red]Only prob I am having thus far is that only one core shows up in the Task Manager. [/COLOR]In [COLOR=DarkRed]**Ubuntu**[/COLOR] and **[COLOR=DarkGreen]Mint[/COLOR]**, its always been four cores for my Core i3, even though technically it has two cores.

Any thoughts on what to do? Does only the 64bit edition of Lubuntu support more cores?


Hi,

The "**[COLOR=Navy]L[/COLOR]**" in "[COLOR=Navy]**L**[/COLOR][COLOR=DarkRed]ubuntu[/COLOR]" means **[COLOR=Navy]L[/COLOR]**ight (LXDE = Lightweight X11 Desktop Environemnt); therefore, most if not all the default applications must be lightweight too otherwise, Lubuntu will not be so much different than Ubuntu :)

Having the said, if you are not happy with the default System Monitor or Task Manager, please run this from LXTerminal

```
sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get install gnome-system-monitor
```

Done :D

With Linux, anything and everything is POSSIBLE. Don't let the system control or limit you from doing what you want. One of the things I adore about Linux rather than its name (Windows? Doors maybe? :P ) is the fact that it's just like Lego, you build it the way YOU want :)

Check the screenshot and by the way, PLEASE don't freak out regarding the memory, I have many applications opened plus two browsers, with minimum 7 or 8 tabs :P

---

### Post by Rodney9 on 2011-10-29
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=11407207#post11407207](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=11407207#post11407207)

I was looking for a better and more reliable appointment calendar.

[Sunbird]("http://www.mozilla.org/projects/calendar/sunbird/") looks good, it is a stand alone calendar, will need to be added to auto start, it also quite light weight.

I have upgraded Sylpheed to Claws mail for it's extra functionality and it is still very light.

Claws has a plugin called [vCalendar]("http://www.claws-mail.org/plugin.php?plugin=vcalendar"), mostly meant for meetings, but has alarms.

So I will trial both.

### Post by mörgæs on 2011-10-29
Here is some advice for installing on **really** old computers.

Sometimes the computer can run Lubuntu once installed on the hard drive, but the normal installation process itself might be too heavy. In that case:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=9834517&postcount=261](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=9834517&postcount=261)

The method is also a good option, if the CD drive is partly failing, since it only reads 15-20 MB from the CD.

### Post by KBD47 on 2011-10-30
Great job amjjawad!
A couple quick suggestions, for those looking for power adjustments, you can right-click on the battery icon to access the settings. For those like me who find the shutdown icon to be in the way on the lower right corner of the desktop, you can remove it by right-clicking on it and choosing "remove". I find my cursor is almost on top of it whenever I'm scrolling down a web page, always afraid I'll accidentally click on it.The button is redundant as you have the same option under your menu at the left under 'log out'. My suggestion would be to leave it off of future versions of Lubuntu.
Best Wishes.
KBD47

### Post by Orographic on 2011-10-30
A couple of quick things:

Screen saver question: What does 'cycle after' mean in settings? I would prefer to blank the screen but not turn it off.

Menu Question:

Is there any way to change the 'log out' option in the menu to 'shut down'? Just to make it easier for my wife when using this computer. 


Thanks again for all the work that has been put into Lubuntu. I'm pretty much using it full time on my first generation Core i3, H55 system. I can run Ubuntu, Kubuntu and Fedora but Lubuntu is faster/smoother and I don't really like Unity or Gnome 3. Unity and Gnome 3 feel like big buttoned, smart phone screens for me but with less customisations...

Lubuntu is very good indeed.

---

### Post by Rodney9 on 2011-10-30
> **Orographic said:**
> A couple of quick things:

Screen saver question: What does 'cycle after' mean in settings? I would prefer to blank the screen but not turn it off.

Menu Question:

Is there any way to change the 'log out' option in the menu to 'shut down'? Just to make it easier for my wife when using this computer. 


Thanks again for all the work that has been put into Lubuntu. I'm pretty much using it full time on my first generation Core i3, H55 system. I can run Ubuntu, Kubuntu and Fedora but Lubuntu is faster/smoother and I don't really like Unity or Gnome 3. Unity and Gnome 3 feel like big buttoned, smart phone screens for me but with less customisations...

Lubuntu is very good indeed.

'cycle after' means how long between different screen savers will show if you have 'Random Screen Saver' selected.

You can just blank the screen in the 'Screen Saver Preferences' 'Display Modes' 'Modes'

When I click the 'Log Out' in the menu or on the panel I get the menu for Shutdown, Reboot, Suspend etc. I think it is safer this way, if it went straight to shutdown you could click it by mistake to easily.

I agree Lubuntu is terrific, so fast and so sleek.

Rodney

---

### Post by dajare on 2011-10-30
I've done a little looking, and feel like I ought to know the answer to this ... but I don't:

**Is there a way to find out which apps are already available for Lubuntu from its Synaptic Package Manager without being "in" Lubuntu?**

I've been doing some Live CD sessions, and will be switching over when I get a bit of free time, but meanwhile would like to be able to do investigating about available packages.

Can someone point me in the right direction? *Thanks!*

---

### Post by Rodney9 on 2011-10-30
> **dajare said:**
> I've done a little looking, and feel like I ought to know the answer to this ... but I don't:

**Is there a way to find out which apps are already available for Lubuntu from its Synaptic Package Manager without being "in" Lubuntu?**

I've been doing some Live CD sessions, and will be switching over when I get a bit of free time, but meanwhile would like to be able to do investigating about available packages.

Can someone point me in the right direction? *Thanks!*

You can use "Filters" in Synaptic, go to 'Settings' ' Filters' (see below) and make a new one clicking on 'New' then select what you want to see or not.
Once that's done go to 'Custom Filters' and select yours.

Make sure you check out the  ["Lubuntu One Stop Group"]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=11410340#post11410340")

---

Your answer is right there.

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-10-30
> **Rodney9 said:**
> You can use "Filters" in Synaptic, go to 'Settings' ' Filters' (see below) and make a new one clicking on 'New' then select what you want to see or not.
Once that's done go to 'Custom Filters' and select yours.

Make sure you check out the  ["Lubuntu One Stop Group"]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=11410340#post11410340")

Yes, that will show all the packages + applications.
It helps if someone really knows what he/she is looking for but it might not help those who want to take a quick overview of what is going on.

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-10-30
> **KBD47 said:**
> Great job amjjawad!

Appreciate that indeed :)

> For those like me who find the shutdown icon to be in the way on the lower right corner of the desktop, you can remove it by right-clicking on it and choosing "remove". I find my cursor is almost on top of it whenever I'm scrolling down a web page, always afraid I'll accidentally click on it.The button is redundant as you have the same option under your menu at the left under 'log out'. **My suggestion would be to leave it off of future versions of Lubuntu**.I tend to disagree, I'm afraid. Why? because when you accidentally click that button, you'll have more options than just "Shutdown". Log out, Restart, Shut down, Suspend and Hibernate. So please, don't be afraid at all :)
However, Lubuntu is very flexible, **you **can remove it or move it.

For me, I did a workaround to add "Lock Screen" right next to my Shutdown button on Lubuntu 11.04 - on the guides section, you'll find a HOWTO for that :)

Thank you for your suggestion :)

---

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-10-30
> **mörgæs said:**
> Here is some advice for installing on **really** old computers.

Sometimes the computer can run Lubuntu once installed on the hard drive, but the normal installation process itself might be too heavy. In that case:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=9834517&postcount=261](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=9834517&postcount=261)

The method is also a good option, if the CD drive is partly failing, since it only reads 15-20 MB from the CD.

Luckily, my 2nd Test PC has 512MB Physical Memory and I can drop that down till 256MB. I'm going to try that but if it needs a LAN connection, then I'm afraid I can't :(
I'm connecting through Wireless Range Extender because I'm too far from the Router.

### Post by KBD47 on 2011-11-01
Faenza icons look nice in Lubuntu. They can be installed via terminal then chosen under settings for 'customize look and feel' and chosen under icons.


    sudo add-apt-repository ppa:tiheum/equinox

    sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get install faenza-icon-theme

[http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Faenza?content=128143](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Faenza?content=128143)

Gnome Screenshot can be installed via Synaptic Package Manager to do screenshots in Lubuntu.

### Post by Orographic on 2011-11-02
> **amjjawad said:**
> I'm having insomnia for the last few days and I can't sleep ... it's 6:30am and even when I'm dead tired, I can't sleep ... guess it's Lubuntu's Energy that keeps me awake? don't know :) ...

Sorry to hear that. Its much more important that you get sleep than help here. There are some ideas listed below that will help you sleep. :)

Try and keep your diet simple; no caffeine (coffee, tea, chocolate) or at least non after lunch-time, no artificial preservatives or additives, eat relaxing foods like rolled oats in the evening, reduce your sugar intake. Also, take a calcium and magnesium tablet in the middle of the day and also before bed-time. Exercise for at least half an hour during the day. Massage your forehead, and ears and eyes just before bed for 10 minutes. Don't sit at the computer after 8pm to 9pm. If it persists, see your doctor.

### Post by ohiomoto on 2011-11-02
Great thread!  

I haven't had time to read the whole thing, but I do have a suggestion.  This is going to turn into a HUGE thread, and it will be difficult for amjjawad to manage.  It will be nearly impossible for amjjawad to link together useful solutions that span multiple posts.  So this useful information will eventually get lost in here.  Furthermore it will be difficult for others to follow along because there will be multiple issues being discussed simultaneously.  

I would like to suggest that **users in need of help** do the following:

[LIST=1]
[*]First check the the "Solved Threads" listed in post #3 in this thread.   If you find your solution, great!  If not proceed to step 2.
[*]Start a NEW THREAD to explain your issue!
[*]Post a LINK to your thead here so we can try to help you.  Any discussons pretaining to your issure should stay in that thread.  If someone posts information here, you should copy it into your new thread.  It will be more useful there.
[*]Once your issue is SOLVED, mark is SOLVED!!! Then post here that is was solved so  amjjawad knows to move the thread to the solved thread list in his post.
[/LIST]


I would like to suggest **amjjawad** do the following:
[LIST=1]
[*]Change the "Solved Threads" post to include "Unsolved Threads" as well.
[*]Add these instructions to that thead.  (Edit them to suite your needs of course!)
[*]When you see a new "unsolved" thread, post the link in the "Unsolved Thread " list so we can easily see who needs help!
[*]When you see that someone posts here that their thread was solved, move the link to the "Solved Thread" list.
[/LIST]

Ok, so the list probably needs a little editing, but I think you get the idea.

I hope you can see how this will make this thread more manageable.  Plus it would be better to actually solve the issues in separate threads.  That way people searching the forums will find it more easily. Also, a lot of users won't be able to follow this thread on a daily basis.  By having an "unsolved thread" list, they can quickly see who still needs help.

---

You can add a battery indicator:

Right-click on the taskbar

Choose Panel Settings > Panel Applets > Add

Choose 'Battery Monitor'

Click '+Add'

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-11-04
> **Hylas de Niall said:**
> Hi amjjawad 
Hi and sorry for being late :)

> Last night i resurrected my brother's old Toshiba EA60 -155 laptop using Lubuntu 11.10. He gave me the machine because 'the new battery doesn't charge up, and the graphics more often than not go into an infinite loop on boot-up'. NOW (with Lubuntu) the graphics are rock-solid and the battery is starting to charge up!
Yet again, Lubuntu proves itself as one of the best Distributions with Old and New machines :)
Glad to know that!

> I need a vector graphics program like Inkscape or Xara XS now, i looked at Xara, but that has a list of dependencies as long as my arm to run and i was worried how that would impact on the speed of the machine?
> Unused RAM is wasted RAM. I've seen that somewhere on Arch Wiki. I'm a strong believer in that quote :)

Having many dependencies doesn't mean slower performance . That will be true only if all or most of these dependencies will be loaded in RAM and the CPU has to deal with all of them. 

What are the specifications of your machine?

> If i remember right, Puppy Linux used to come with Ink-Lite a minimal version of Inkscape that ran very well on low-end machines, is there anything similar that will work nicely on Lubuntu?
Most if not all of the applications you can use and run on Ubuntu, you can also use and run on Lubuntu. Sometimes, you just need to do some workaround to get it to work. For example, Compiz can work on LXDE/Lubuntu with some workaround/editing config files. Cairo-Dock on the other hand work out-of-the box, at least with me. Some other programs work without doing anything. Some other need to edit their .desktop file in the applications folder (/usr/share/applicaitons) to show them on the Menu.

If I were you, I would go ahead and install that particular application and see how well or bad it will work on Lubuntu or any other system that I'm using.
Why you want to do that? two good reasons:

1- When you do that yourself, you will learn and that information will stick in your mind and you will never forget it. It's the best way of learning - this is how I learned almost everything by myself.

2- Helping others by advices, guides, etc. We need to help Linux Community to grow bigger and be better. For me, I see it's my duty to return the favour to Linux (which gave me a solid amazing OS to use and changed my entire life) by helping its users.

I hope you see my point :)

> Keep up the good work!
I promise I'll ;)

By the way, I see the need of a new guide is increasing on daily basis. Another friend also suggested that. So, I'll work on a new guide to explain more about the Applications you can use with Lubuntu. People should never be afraid or worry too much ... I mean for God's sake this is Linux not Windows and it's so easy to fix things in Linux :) I'm saying that from experience :)

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-11-04
> **lazylew said:**
> That explains - thanks for the tip. I'll stick with 10.04 and Xubuntu for now then; Lubuntu will be explored carefully bit by bit :-) (can always replace PCMan if I like it, or upgrade to 11.10)

Hi again :)

May I share an advice or tip I have learned myself?

> Don't let anything stop you from learning/exploring new things and from having fun by doing that :)

I have learned that, specially with Linux.
Having that said, why to wait? why to stick with one option (even if that option works perfectly with you) while there are many other options might be even better?

If you don't have a spare machine, if you don't want to mess around with your only machine, try to install Lubuntu or any other system in mind into USB Drive. Yes, it will be slower but hey, you are not messing around with your main system at all. Check the first post, there is a guide of HOWTO install Lubuntu on USB Drive.

That what I would do :)

I have Xubuntu installed on a test machine and I dropped the RAM to 256MB (but it says 242MB). I have it with:
Mint LXDE 11
Lubuntu 11.10
Peppermint 2
CrunchBang 10
ArchBang 102011

I don't really like Xubuntu/XFCE and I don't see it lightweight. The performance is slow on such RAM while LXDE runs faster.
I'm just trying to find out why users are so in love with Xubuntu beside I want to do some other tests.

If you don't have two PCs like me, as I mentioned above, USB Drives are not expensive these days :)

I'll try to figure out HOWTO Replace PCManFM with another File Manager and once I do that, I'll write a guide about it and post it here. However, if truth to be told, I prefer something much better. Why to replace? why not to improve what I current have installed by default? I have many ideas for PCManFM and if the developers fail to do that list of needs, then, I may think to replace PCManFM.

This is my personal approach that, again, I learned while using Linux and I'm just sharing it with you and everyone else. 

Thank you :)

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-11-06
[CENTER][COLOR=Blue][B][SIZE=4]HOW TO Search for [COLOR=Navy]Lubuntu[/COLOR] Threads on [COLOR=Sienna]Ubuntu Forum[/COLOR]?
[/SIZE][/B][/COLOR][/CENTER]



[LIST]
[*] From your **User CP** Page, Click on **Search** and then **Advanced Search**
[*]You could use the first box on the left "**Search by Keyword**". Just type "**Lubuntu**" then **Search Now**.
[*]You could also use another Search Options. However, please note that some users, by mistake, choose for example **[lubuntu]** prefix while their thread is talking about Ubuntu. Some other users may use [COLOR=DarkRed]**[ubuntu]**[/COLOR] prefix but their thread is talking about Lubuntu.
[*]You could also use "**Search by Tag**".
[/LIST]

Please see the attached Screenshots.

If you couldn't find what you are looking for on [Post #3]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=11358669&postcount=3") on this thread, please search the forum as explained above.

In General, you could also use: **[www.googlubuntu.com]("http://www.googlubuntu.com")** which will send you back to the forum in most cases ;)

[B]With the rapid growth of this thread and the importance of it, I think it's time to create [COLOR=Red]HOWTO Use Lubuntu One Stop Thread[/COLOR] so there you go :)
[/B]
[U][B]
Introduction:
[/B][/U]Lubutnu's Team is keen to improve Lubuntu and make it works out-of-the box. However, nothing is perfect and some users may find some hard time dealing with Lubuntu, specially new comers. This guide and of course this thread should make your life easier and help you as much as possible :)


[U][B]Steps you need to follow to make life easier:
[/B][/U]
[LIST=1]
[*]Read **[the first post]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=11254865&postcount=1")** of this thread.
[*]There are lots of useful links that might help you to answer any question or solve any problem.
[*]If you couldn't find what you are looking for in the first post and all its section, please check **[post #3]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=11358669&postcount=3")**. Post #3 will explain to you what you need to do. You will have two options, either to search on the listed threads OR search Ubuntu Forum for similar questions/problems.
[*]Yet again, if you couldn't find what you are looking for, please do some google search or use [www.googlubuntu.com]("http://www.googlubuntu.com")
[*]Remember, there is **[LXDE Forum]("http://forum.lxde.org/")**, yet another place to look into.
[*]If all the above steps failed to answer your question(s) or solve your problem(s), please do one simple thing:
[/LIST]

[LIST]
[*]**[COLOR=Red]_Start_ a New Thread [/COLOR]**in the right section or sub-forum ([Absolute Beginner Talk]("http://ubuntuforums.org/forumdisplay.php?f=326"), [General Help]("http://ubuntuforums.org/forumdisplay.php?f=331"), [etc]("http://ubuntuforums.org/index.php")).
[*]**[SIZE=4][COLOR=DarkRed]Please, have a look at this guide [here]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=11532952&postcount=349").[/COLOR][/SIZE]**
[*]If NO ONE get back to you shortly, please **[COLOR=Red]FEEL FREE to PM me THE LINK of Your New Thread[/COLOR]**. I'll be more than glad to help :)
[*]Remember, you can use the [COLOR=Red]**IRC Channel**[/COLOR] for a faster answer but since I'm a forum type of guy, I prefer forum support but that's me.
[*]Another [COLOR=Red]**alternative way**[/COLOR] is to register in Launchpad and join [Lubuntu Team on Launchpad]("https://launchpad.net/%7Elubuntu-desktop"). You can send an email to the team and get an answer. However, yet again, I think forum has more traffic than any other help/support channel.
[*]**[COLOR=Navy]Please do your best to contribute to this thread. Post whatever may add a value and others will be glad to know. After all, we are all here to help and learn[/COLOR]**.
[/LIST]

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-11-10
> **dajare said:**
> I've done a forum search on this one, but can't find an answer....

In my old system (Jaunty), I used Leafpad a lot, and it had a [quite nice logo](http://tarot.freeshell.org/leafpad/leafpadle.png) which was distinctive.

It's great to have Leafpad as standard in Lubuntu ... but it's got a fairly boring generic "editor" icon, and I'd love to have that nice leafy one back. Are there directions on how to do this? Or should Lubuntu's Leafpad have the "proper" icon as an option somewhere...?

(Not the most important issue ever, but hey! It's nice to have things ... nice!) Thanks for any help with this!

Hi,

I'm on hurry but I found out how to do this :D

1- Download the image you want [http://tarot.freeshell.org/leafpad/leafpadle.png](http://tarot.freeshell.org/leafpad/leafpadle.png)

Save it to downloads folder

2- Open PCManFM > Tools > Open Current Folder as Root

3- Go to: /usr/share/pixmaps/

4- Open a 2nd tab in PCManFM (while you are logged in as root) and go to your downloads folder, copy your leafpad image and paste it in "/usr/share/pixmaps"

5- While you still logged in as root, go to "/usr/share/applications/" and open "leafpad.desktop"

6- Copy and paste this:

```
Icon=leafpadle
#Icon=leafpad
```

Then Save

7- Check Menu > Accessories > Leafpad

8- DONE :D

### Post by mörgæs on 2011-11-12
**The Lubuntu web site**

I noticed that the old [www.lubuntu.net](www.lubuntu.net) web site is up again. I am trying to say 'congratulations', but I can't.

This is not written in order to be rude, but to help Lubuntu: Sorry friends, the web site is missing the target. It does not help a beginner to take the first step into the Lubuntu world.

In a nutshell: A web site should be 'to me' and not 'from you'. The difference is huge, and it takes some time to grasp the full consequences of this.

I have a long experience in building web sites which fail due to language, layout, expectations to the visitor and lack of systematic testing. Now I believe that I have some background for helping people to avoid the worst mistakes. 

It seems like this thread is turning into a general meeting place for Lubuntu, not only a list of solved problems, so I guess it is the place to post. Besides, I have been searching high and low on [www.lubuntu.net](www.lubuntu.net) without finding any web site team to contact.

So: If anyone reading this can set me in touch with people building the Lubuntu site please do so. I am willing to put some effort into getting a better web site.

---

### Post by rojaasensei on 2011-11-13
Just wanted to let everyone know that the following indicators/applets work in Lubuntu 11.10

Caffeine: control screensaver from lxpanel
Lookit: screen capture from lxpanel
Ejecter: safely unmount USB devices from panel
Diodon: clipboard on panel (very handy)
Alarm Clock: from repository, not the plugin, the program, can autostart on panel with session

The first four can be found at [http://askubuntu.com/questions/30334/list-of-application-indicators](http://askubuntu.com/questions/30334/list-of-application-indicators), the last in the Lubuntu Software Centre.

Enjoy:)

---

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-11-13
[B][SIZE=4][COLOR=Red]
HOW TO Change Font Size in [COLOR=Purple]Pidgin[/COLOR]?[/COLOR][/SIZE][/B]

One of my worst nightmare until few minutes ago was HOW TO CHANGE THE FONT? Perhaps you already know that but I just learned how to do it. I never use Pidgin but I had to use it today so there you go.

Well, thanks to Google, I found the package. Now, this is HOWTO do it:


[LIST=1]
[*]From **LXTerminal**, install "pidgin-extprefs" package ```
sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get install pidgin-extprefs
``` OR you can do that from **Synaptic**.
[*]Open **[COLOR=Purple]Pidgin[/COLOR]**.
[*]**Tools > Plugins** OR **Ctrl+U** while Pidgin Window is Highlighted
[*]See these Screen-shots:
[/LIST]

[IMG]http://i42.tinypic.com/2lc63bm.jpg[/IMG]


Click on "**Configure Plugin**"



[IMG]http://i42.tinypic.com/5jwb6g.jpg[/IMG]


Don't forget to pray for me :P

---

[SIZE=6]**Bugs Reported**[/SIZE]
**[COLOR=Red]New Entry that will contain the bugs reported by Users[/COLOR]**


[LEFT]Hello and Welcome to this NEW Entry :)

In this section/entry that I'll update on regular basis, I'm going to post the links of the reported bugs that myself or any other Lubuntu User will report. This will definitely help everyone to stay up-to-date with what is going on and to save everyone's time. Instead of starting new thread or asking whether it's a bug or not, this post will be the answer to such Qs. However, I'm not saying this is everything. This is NOT a replacement for Launchpad NOR Google. It's just a shortcut, that's all :)


[SIZE=4][U][B]List of Reported Bugs:
[/B][/U][/SIZE]
[LIST=1]
[*][https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/pcmanfm/+bug/891020](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/pcmanfm/+bug/891020)

### Post by Dennis N on 2011-11-16
> **rezbd said:**
> my problem is so simple that I've decided to post it here.

I'm missing an icon (shutdown/logout) on my Lubuntu desktop panel:

[[IMG]http://img695.imageshack.us/img695/9652/79347593.png[/IMG]]("http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/695/79347593.png/")  Uploaded with [ImageShack.us]("http://imageshack.us")

somehow I've removed it. I've tried "Add/remove panel items" but couldn't restore it. how can I get it back please? thank you.

One way to fix this is to restore the default panel. There may be other ways. This is from an old thread written before the current version of Lubuntu. (I know it works for Lubuntu 11.04, where I had the same problem). 

Original Thread:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1490938](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1490938)

From Post #11 in that thread:

Move the old panel file out in case you want to reference it for your custom configs.

```
mv ~/.config/lxpanel/Lubuntu/panels/panel ~/
```

Restart lxpanel

```
lxpanelctl restart
```

Now we have default panel configuration including Shutdown button
Notice config file panel is not created until you change the default panel configuration.

---

problem solved by restoring the default panel.

### Post by MG&amp;TL on 2011-11-17
Two things: your monitor size. If you've got high resolution, but small screen, you can see where this is going. Go to 'monitor' in preferences and change there.

Other thing: you change font size here: lxmenu -> Preferences -> Openbox configuration manager -> appearance.

And thanks for giving it a go. :D

### Post by Dennis N on 2011-11-17
> **Psyael said:**
> I need help.

I just installed Lubuntu and my system fonts are extremely tiny. I'm using an NVidia GTX460 with the proprietary drivers and 1080 resolution. Fonts in Chromium (i.e. this web page) are fine, but the fonts in tooltips etc are system standard miniature.


As far as I know, the only way to increase the size of the font used on the panel's task bar (window list) at this time is to increase the panel width and icon size in "panel settings". At some icon size settings, the font size increases.

Desktop icons - this font can be changed through "Desktop Preferences" (right-click on desktop).

All the other possible font size/style changes can be done in the "Customize Look and Feel" dialog under Main Menu > Preferences.

In that dialog,

**Widget Tab**: "default font" setting box controls fonts in window menus, the main menu, and tool tips. (It will also control the font face in the task bar, but the size will not change.)
**Window Border Tab > Title Bar Tab**: (obviously) controls the active and inactive window title bar fonts.

This has been the response so far:

'Our bug bot has marked this as a bug against the plymouth package. The
message is related to plymouth, but we have not in general heard reports
of this problem with Ubuntu 11.10. We *have* heard of such things on
Lubuntu in particular. So there seems to be something wrong in the
Lubuntu startup sequence that causes plymouth to be killed earlier than
it should be.'

Hi,

[IMG]http://i43.tinypic.com/2m2jdcj.jpg[/IMG]


What happens in my case is when I move the mouse to stop the screensaver, I see my desktop then after less than 1 second the screensaver resumes again so I have to stop it all over again. I Killed one of these two process and it seems OK now.

### Post by jontheid on 2011-11-29
I cured the problem of having two xscreensavers by doing this:

Open /etc/xdg/lxsession/Lubuntu/autostart using leafpad as root

delete the line @xscreensaver, and save the file.

Create a file called 'xscreensaver.desktop' using leafpad 

Paste this into it:

[Desktop Entry]
Exec=xscreensaver -no-splash
Name=XScreenSaver
Type=Application

Save this file in /etc/xdg/autostart

It works for me! I don't know why it works but it does.
Cheers
Jon

---

### Post by jontheid on 2011-11-29
One of the nice things about having autostarted applications in 
/etc/xdg/autostart is that the 'desktop session settings' applications under 'preferences' displays these applications in the 'automatically started applications' tab and you can turn them on or off with just clicking a box.

'desktop session settings' does not display any of the applications autostarted by /etc/xdg/lxsession/Lubuntu/autostart or /home/username/.config/autostart/

---

### Post by KBD47 on 2011-11-29
For those who like a 12 hour clock with am/pm right click on the clock, go to settings, and in the top box put this:
%I:%M %p

---

### Post by Rex Bouwense on 2011-11-29

### Post by Big Lizard on 2011-11-30
Here is the code I use. 

```
%a %b %e ~ %I:%M %p
```And it looks like this.

[IMG]http://i813.photobucket.com/albums/zz59/knebworth79/HOLD/MyClock.jpg[/IMG]



Here is a link for all the different codes for the clock configuration.

[http://linux.about.com/library/cmd/blcmdln_clock.htm](http://linux.about.com/library/cmd/blcmdln_clock.htm)

### Post by KBD47 on 2011-12-02
Anyone else have their battery indicator go missing from their panel? I have power manager checked on my startup, and I can add a battery indicator to the panel--ugly little green thing--but my default battery icon is gone. I can't even get xfce4-power-manager to launch from the terminal, but synaptic shows it installed. Anyone have any thoughts?
Thanks.
KBD47
Edit: Not sure why it disappeared, but here is how I fixed it:
in a terminal put:

xfce4-power-manager-settings

when it opens your settings make sure it says:

&#8220;always show icon&#8221;

### Post by Orographic on 2011-12-09
Just wanted to let Lubuntu users know of an issue when using Simple Scan. I just couldn't get it to detect my HP F2280 scanner although the print function on the same printer/scanner was fine.

For some reason Lubuntu 11.10 doesn’t install all of the packages needed for Simple Scan to detect a scanner. Make sure ‘libsane-hpaio’ or similar is installed and this will usually also install 'sane-utils' and 'hplip' as well - these three were missing by default. Then, the scanner should be recognised. 

I worked this out by typing libsane into Mint 11 Synaptic and finding some of the packages that were missing in Lubuntu 11.10. Mint 11 (on this same machine, on another hard drive) recognised my printer/scanner no problems as did Ubuntu Unity. Not sure why Lubuntu didn't install these packages by default...

---

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-12-12
[COLOR=Red][B]_[SIZE=4]NOTE[/SIZE]_: Please note that The Developers don't actually look at forums but instead, they look at Launchpad Reports and Mailing List. In case you want to start a new thread to drag the developers attention, this is NOT the right way.
[/B][/COLOR]

Hi,

I don't know why I didn't think about this before (write this short guide and include it in Lubuntu One Stop Thread) but day after day, I see the same requests from people who are willing to help and support (would you please mention more details about your issue?) while from the users side, those who seek help and support, they still on the wrong page. To make this as simple as possible and as clear as possible, all what you need to is these steps.

I'm sure this has been explained later but as always, I like to do it my way with Lubuntu Style :)

**_[COLOR=Red]NOTE THAT:[/COLOR]_** **Please, DO NOT start a new thread UNLESS you do some google OR [www.googlubuntu.com]("http://www.googlubuntu.com") search. If you think your problem is unique OR you will not find any related information, then there is only one way to find out which is a simple google search that will save a lot from your time as you don't have to wait for anyone to jump in and help**

[B][U]Steps:
[/U][/B]
1- Make sure to choose the correct sub-forum for your thread. There are many sub-forums on Ubuntu Forum. Please have a look her: [http://ubuntuforums.org/index.php](http://ubuntuforums.org/index.php)

2- Make sure to choose the correct "Prefix" for your Thread. I've seen MANY threads starting with **[COLOR=Navy]Lubuntu[/COLOR]** Prefix while these threads have nothing to do with Lubuntu itself.

[IMG]http://i52.tinypic.com/i2ks2s.jpg[/IMG]

3- The Title of your thread is VERY important. Don't write your Life's story but also don't use just one or two words. Be informative as much as you can.


4- Please keep in mind that those who are willing to help and support you are not sitting in front of your monitor/screen. The less details your provide, the less help you get. After all, it's a waste of time if your thread has less needed information.

5- IMHO, there is a list of important details that one should include in his/her thread:

a- What Release of Lubuntu/Ubuntu/Xubuntu/Kubuntu is he/she using?

```
lsb_release -a

```

b- What kind of installation? normal? virtual? wubi (for Ubuntu)?



c- What media he/she has used? Live CD? Live USB? 



d- What iso he/she has downloaded (name of the iso)? 
Which architecture (32-bit or 64-bit)?



e- [MD5SUM checking]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/HowToMD5SUM")? this must be the first step after installing the iso file and before burning the Live CD or Creating the Live USB.
See also: [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/UbuntuHashes](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/UbuntuHashes)



f- What application he/she has used to create the Live CD or Live USB?

**[COLOR=Red]Recommendations[/COLOR]**: 
Please make sure to burn the image (iso file) at the minimum speed - I suggest 8x. K3b is my favorite but YMMV. 

In case of Live USB, [UNetbootin]("http://unetbootin.sourceforge.net/") is highly recommended.



g- Probably, this should be the first information on a new thread. Hardware Details/Specifications of the machine.

```
sudo lshw

```This will give you all the details you may need.



h- What Kernel?

```
uname -r
```[B][COLOR=red]Tip:
[/COLOR][/B]
It's highly recommended to do:
```
sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get upgrade

```right after you are done with the installation.


i- In case of potential bug, make sure you can re-produce that. Don't assume it's a bug just like that. Sometimes, some issues can be solved easily.



j- Details, details and details are very important. Also, please make sure to mention the steps you followed to fix the issue.



k- Finally, PLEASE make sure to follow these simple and basic steps when posting:

1- Please, make sure to use "CODE" tags when posting any output from Terminal:

[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/picture.php?albumid=2161&pictureid=8148[/IMG]



2- If you want to include a screenshot which is hosted on one of the free websites (like tinypic.com), you can do that easily:

[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/picture.php?albumid=2161&pictureid=8147[/IMG]



3- Want to include your screenshot as an attachment:

[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/picture.php?albumid=2161&pictureid=8046[/IMG]

[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/picture.php?albumid=2161&pictureid=8047[/IMG]



4- Help others by marking your thread as SOLVED in case your issue is fixed. Remember, you can always set it as UNSOLVED in case you need to add more Qs.

[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/picture.php?albumid=2161&pictureid=7263[/IMG]



Hope this will be helpful. Enjoy ;)

---

> Ladies and Gentlemen, Lubuntu Software Center 0.0.2 is out!
this is the first stable version, you can grab the tarball at [http://launchpad.net/lubuntu-software-center](http://launchpad.net/lubuntu-software-center)
Now we need your tests, you comments and your hints.

Regards

Stephen Smally

P.S. the PPA is always updated, but is recommended only for test.

More information:


```
sudo apt-add-repository ppa:lubuntu-desktop/ppa

```
```
sudo apt-get update

```
```
sudo apt-get install lubuntu-software-center

```

You can also download and install from here: [https://launchpad.net/lubuntu-software-center](https://launchpad.net/lubuntu-software-center)

Your help is highly appreciated. If you are willing to help, please download, install, test and report to Launchpad in case of bugs. REMEMBER, the developers don't actually look at this forum :)

### Post by amjjawad on 2011-12-18
Lubuntu Developers are doing their best to provide and deliver the best to Lubuntu Users. I think, IMHO, instead of using GNOME Screenshot or Shutter, it's better to use LXDE/Lubuntu Applications. I'm not saying these are prefect because NOTHING is prefect but by using these apps, you are HELPING out. The more you use, the more feedback/bugs will pop up every now and then and eventually, all that will help these apps to get better.

To add LXScreenshot, you need to add lubuntu-desktop ppa.

Here is how:

1- ```
sudo add-apt-repository ppa:lubuntu-desktop/ppa
```

2- ```
sudo apt-get update
```

3- ```
sudo apt-get install lxscreenshot
```

4- Done. You'll find it: Menu > Accessories > LXScreenshot

Enjoy :)

### Post by MG&amp;TL on 2011-12-18
I think everyone's missing the point a little here, amjjawad made the announcement partly from a news perspective, and partly because he wants to make sure that 12.04 is the best yet. You can all help this by testing it. I can assure you nothing is going to 'mess up your system', and if you are that paranoid, but still want to help, get a copy with bzr and run it without it installing anything. :)

I am one of three developers of LSC. (ok, two developers, (one rubbish-me!) and one packager/translation handler/release manager extraodinaire) and the work is enormous.  The vala port, for instance, currently fails to compile with a total of 256 errors. You can help by testing major, stable releases to find obscure bugs that we haven't had time to find.

Thank you, Rex, for testing unstable stuff, :D, but the point to others was that you can now get it with reduced risk of mess-ups (not that there was much to start with).

This is not a 'dev thread'-they don't exist. Oh yeah, and we're not saying you *have* to try it, but it would be nice to give back, wouldn't it? 

Peace, all.

### Post by amjjawad on 2012-01-17
[PCManFM]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PCMan_File_Manager") is the default File Manager in Lubuntu. It happens sometimes that PCManFM crashes or acting crazy so in order to check what is wrong and track the issue, you need, just like we used to do with other application, to open it from the terminal and see what is the output will be. However, running PCManFM from LXTerminal is not straightforward so this is how to do this. 

> PCManFM runs as a daemon and manages your desktop, so when you run it from a terminal it will simply open the PCManFM file manager window instead of starting a new session. You will need to 'killall pcmanfm'
and then run 'pcmanfm --desktop --profile=lubuntu'

To do the above:

1- Menu > Accessories > LXTerminal

2- Run this command: 
```
killall pcmanfm
```
If you have icons on your Desktop, these will be gone when you kill PCManFM so don't panic, you'll see them again :)

3- Run this command: 
```
pcmanfm --desktop --profile=lubuntu
```
Keep LXTerminal on, don't close it.

4- Now, do whatever you used to do. If there is something wrong, LXTerminal will show everything. 

5- To report bugs for PCManFM: [http://sourceforge.net/tracker/?group_id=156956&atid=801864](http://sourceforge.net/tracker/?group_id=156956&atid=801864)

OR

You can click on "Report Problem" when PCManFM crashes and you see the crash report (Application Problem).

Hope that will help :)

Thanks!

### Post by Paul A C on 2012-03-01
I have **added** Nautilus as a second file manager to my Lubuntu machines.  I still use PCManFm mostly, but resort to Nautilus when I want to set up shares and the like, since that is the way I first learnt to do it.  Very seldom I use Nautilus except for that, since PCManFM does pretty well all else I want.

I also sometimes start pcmanfm using gksudo

> gksudo pcmanfm.  Doing that gives the familiar file manager with sudo rights, great for updating permissions and copying system files and so forth.  (Of course easy to trash your system too).

What I like so much about Lubuntu is it is so fast even on ancient PCs.  This one is a P3 1Ghz with 384M ram, and it flies!

No excuse not to have a second PC for trying things out on.  Just go to a council scrap yard, junk shop or whatever, and pick up an old PC for nothing.  If it turns on, chances are you can get Lubuntu to run!

---

### Post by Paul A C on 2012-03-02

### Post by amjjawad on 2012-04-11
Since 2010 until now, I think I have done more than 100 installations for Ubuntu and/or Lubuntu but never faced the issue when you got stuck for 1-2 mins on Lubuntu Splash Screen with the 5 dots and a message saying:
```
waiting for network configuration
```then:
```
waiting an additional 60 seconds for network configuration
```And all that while I was done from this: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=11832431&postcount=152](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=11832431&postcount=152)

By the way, YES, that OLD machine is working now with Lubuntu 11.10 and I will write another simple HOWTO to explain how to install Lubuntu on machines with 64MB of RAM :)

I did a search on Google and found some [**messed up threads**]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1859799") with many users posting at the same time without a direct and clear solution for this issue. The most recent thread was for this year and has only 3 posts so I posted there: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1946216](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1946216)

Since I do have the same issue and I promised that user to find a fix, I guess I did find already and, as usual, I thought it is better to document this so there you go:

Because I fixed that on a very old machine, I decided to go the CLI and Alt+Ctrl+F2 approach so YOU ARE FREE to do that while you are logged in to the GUI :) - Okay, I will write the general steps so feel free to use whatever approach you like.

1- ```
sudo nano /etc/network/interfaces
```*[COLOR=Red]If you are typing this from LXTerminal while logged in to the GUI then:[/COLOR]*
```
gksudo leafpad /etc/network/interfaces
```2- Remove whatever written there and _**just keep**_ this:
```

auto lo
iface lo inet loopback
```[B][COLOR=Red]It is very good idea to keep a backup copy of "interfaces" file just in case so please make sure to save a "interfaces.bak" file before you do anything ;)
[/COLOR][/B]
3- **Ctrl + O** if you are using nano and **Ctrl + S** (File > Save) if you are using leafpad.

4- **Ctrl + X** if you are using nano and **Ctrl + Q** (File > Quit) if you are using leafpad.

5- Reboot.

6- Done.


On my old machine (HP OmniBook 4150), the booting became much faster now :)

Enjoy!

---

I then tried something  else, added under  menuname Office name, and did a copy of one whole   <menu></menu>, just changed under <name></name>   to Office, but it did not appear after save and restart. ---

### Post by spiralciric on 2012-04-14
Ok, figured this on my own.
/usr/share/desktop-directories holds .desktop files, rename them to rename tabs, and also edit them with leafpad and change Name
/etc/xdg/lxlauncher/gtkrc - change tab and font colors
/etc/xdg/menus/lxlauncher... - under category change what is inside that  tab, and change <Directory> to point to file in  desktop-directories to change icon and name.

Still there is no way to change background color or use a wallpaper for  version 2.2. I saw this working for v1.6, but trust me, its not worth  bothering.

Hope this helps someone, it would be nice if someone would add this to lxde wiki under lxlauncher.

---

### Post by Herpythebrony on 2012-04-16
A question I have about Lubuntu is how come Lubuntu get's it's own software center? Why not use the regular Ubuntu software center that comes with the rest of the derivatives?

---

### Post by amjjawad on 2012-04-16
> **Herpythebrony said:**
> A question I have about Lubuntu is how come Lubuntu get's it's own software center? Why not use the regular Ubuntu software center that comes with the rest of the derivatives?

Very GOOD question :D

Simply, because Lubuntu Developers decided to offer yet another alternative to new comers, specially those who are new to Linux and came from Windows, to install the application that want to without the real need of learning little bit about Synaptic or learn little more about Terminal and CLI. And since it's been designed to run on Lubuntu to begin with and Lubuntu meant to be as light as possible, thus LSC (Lubuntu Software Center) will be the 3rd option beside Synaptic and LXTerminal :)

You are FREE to install whatever Software Center you like as long as your machine is capable of running it ;)

We, at Lubuntu Team, we make sure each and every running application MUST be as light as possible. This is our main focus :)

LSC will NOT replace Synaptic by the way :)

---

### Post by MG&amp;TL on 2012-04-21
All memory will (or there would be a serious problem!) be returned to the operating system when the application dies. I believe "leaking" memory is something else, whereby long-running programs use memory and then don't deallocate it, eventually leading to massive RAM use. I think it's more likely that your system is caching some of it for disk caching-[http://www.linuxatemyram.com/]("http://www.linuxatemyram.com/")

Of course, if you've already read that page, it's possible that the application is still shutting down. Browsers are heavy applications.

---

### Post by Frank Moore on 2012-04-22
Dear Lubuntu Developers,

 I have been using Lubuntu since the 10.10 edition. The one with Firefox & Aqualung installed. I like the simple, clean & fast Lxde interface & have been using Lubuntu on my netbooks. 

 I recently acquired a new netbook (Intel Classmate Converter NL2) & my vendor was good enough to send me one of these machines without a preinstalled OS. I was thereby able to avoid paying a licencing fee for an OS I didn't want. I had a thumb-drive with a live install of Lubuntu 11.04 on it so I took this for a test drive. Liking the perfomance (it even responded reasonably well to the stylus on the computer's touchscreen) I made a full installation of Lubuntu. I configured my desktop & installed applications to suit my needs. All went well.

 Then I decided to update my installation to Lubuntu 11.10 in readiness for the forthcoming release of 12.04. It is then that I came across a serious issue that needs to be raised. The battery monitor applet that I used to let my computer know what to do when I close the lid is gone. Before the 'upgrade' closing the lid on my netbook suspended the machine (put it to sleep). This is no longer the case. Two nights in a row I closed the lid on my netbook only to find it still running in the morning. If this had been a month or so ago, at the height of our Australian summer, the consequences could have been dire. The same is true if I had slipped the machine ito its neoprene sleeve & into a backpack to go out.

 I have installed the battery monitor applet from the panel preferences dialogue & checked out the options under the screensaver options. Neither gives the required functionality. What are you people thinking? You advertise your distribution as netbook friendly. Not if it cooks your users' netbooks & creates a fire hazard. I now have to shut my netbook down before putting it in a bag & go through a lengthy restart if I want to use it.

 It was one thing finding myself without an essential like a PDF reader & very useful software such as G-Parted after the upgrade & then having to reinstall all of my codecs & drivers. But the situation with power management is ludicrous. Have the considerations in Lubuntu 12.04 been more practical or are you continuing this blind pursuit of a certain 'look' over function? Surely you have seen what has happened to your parent Ubuntu when they stopped listening to the needs of their users in the pusuit of a trendy looking desktop? We are interested in how our machines work - not the latest ozone theme!

 Finally, is there an application that I can install to replace my battery monitor & power management functionality or should I be looking at another distro, perhaps Linux Mint? Please give these matters some consideration. I'm sure I am not the only person out here who is looking for a small & light OS that maintains a consistent functionality from one release to the next.

yours sincerely,
frank moore.
21-04-2012.
:confused:

---

### Post by amjjawad on 2012-04-26
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]Announced by: [/FONT][/COLOR][LEFT][COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial][B]Julien Lavergne 
[/B][/FONT][/COLOR][/LEFT]
26-04-2012 @12:13 GMT[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]
[/FONT][/COLOR]> [COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]Lubuntu 12.04 is now available :[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * [/FONT][/COLOR][http://cdimage.ubuntu.com/lubuntu/releases/12.04/release/](http://cdimage.ubuntu.com/lubuntu/releases/12.04/release/)
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]
== What is Lubuntu ? ==[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]Lubuntu is a flavor of Ubuntu based on the Lightweight X11 Desktop[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]Environment (LXDE), as its default GUI.  The goal is to provide a very[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]lightweight distribution, with all the advantages of the Ubuntu world[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial](repositories, support, etc.). Lubuntu is targeted at "normal" PC and[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]laptop users running on low-spec hardware. Such users may not know how[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]to use command line tools, and in most cases they just don't have enough[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]resources for all the bells and whistles of the "full-featured"[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]mainstream distributions.[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]With many LXDE components, Lubuntu also uses well-known applications,[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]such as Chromium, Openbox, Pidgin, to name a few. The Lubuntu project[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]wiki contains more information on the project and the applications used[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]available.[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]Unlike Ubuntu, Lubuntu 12.04 is not a LTS, this version will be[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]supported for 18 months. However, a lot of work has been done to improve[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]the stability of the system.[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]== Features ==[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * Based on the lightweight LXDE desktop environment.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * Pcmanfm 0.9.10, a fast and lightweight files manager using gio/gvfs.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * Openbox, the fast and extensible, default windows-manager of LXDE.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * Lightdm, using the simple GTK greeter[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * Chromium, the open-source version of Google Chrome.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * ... and, of course, based on Ubuntu 12.04 LTS.[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]See the complete list of applications on[/FONT][/COLOR]
[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu/Applications](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu/Applications)


[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]== Improvements since Lubuntu 11.10 ==[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * A new software-center, optimized to be lightweight, for easy[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]installation and removal of applications from your system.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * New theme is used, and each previous themes are available in the[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]repositories.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * Lightdm is used as the display manager with the default gtk greeter.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * Blueman is now used instead of gnome-bluetooth for managing bluetooth[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]devices.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * A lot of bug fixes, especially on the panel and the file manager.[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]== Releases notes and known issues ==[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]The release notes, with a list of known problems are available on[/FONT][/COLOR]
[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PrecisePangolin/ReleaseNotes/Lubuntu](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PrecisePangolin/ReleaseNotes/Lubuntu)


[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]== Reporting bugs ==[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]You can find information on how to report a bug on this wiki page :[/FONT][/COLOR]
[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu/ReportingBugs](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu/ReportingBugs)

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]== Thanks ==[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]A big thank to everyone involving in the development of this new great[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]release : LXDE developers, Ubuntu developers, ISO testers, artwork and[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]design people, social-network & blog writers, support & IRC keepers ...[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]It's another success of a great team work :-)[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial]== Links ==[/FONT][/COLOR]

[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * Website : [/FONT][/COLOR][http://lubuntu.net/](http://lubuntu.net/)
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * Documentation : [/FONT][/COLOR][https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu)
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * LXDE website : [/FONT][/COLOR][http://lxde.org/](http://lxde.org/)
[COLOR=#222222][FONT=arial] * Announcement: [/FONT][/COLOR][https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu/Announcement/12.04](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu/Announcement/12.04)[COLOR=Red][B]PLEASE remember that if you  already have Lubuntu 12.04 beta or RC installed, then you don't really  have to download the new ISO and go through the long process yet again  (download, check MD5SUM, etc etc) ... you can just:
 
[/B][/COLOR]```
**  sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get upgrade
```**[COLOR=Red][B]
 
 Enjoy :D

### Post by Adarzh on 2012-04-26

Thanks
Adarsh.

---

### Post by amjjawad on 2012-04-26
> **Adarzh said:**
> How can i upgrade Lubuntu from 11.10 to 12.04.....In the update manager, it shows upgrade to Ubuntu 12.04 and not Lubuntu. If i starts that which one will be installed Ubuntu or Lubuntu.

Thanks
Adarsh.

[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu#Upgrading_from_11.10](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu#Upgrading_from_11.10)

Lubuntu is using the same core system as Ubuntu: [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu#Lubuntu_VS_Ubuntu](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu#Lubuntu_VS_Ubuntu)

You can use whatever approach you want. Either to upgrade via The Update Manager or via LXTerminal.

Note that: you need to backup your important files just in case something might go wrong.
It's also recommended to have a separate /home partition.

### Post by Borunco on 2012-04-26
> **pdlethbridge said:**
> My question did seem a littl strange. I have been running Ububntu for a long time and will sometimes add things to try something diffwerent. I really don.t like unity and niether does my Pc.So after up grading to ubuntu 12.04 I went and added lubuntu using synaptic. I did the same thing a while back[COLOR=Blue] [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1874807](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1874807)[/COLOR]. The end result for me was to get rid of Ubuntu and do a clean install of Lubuntu. If you still want to keep Ubuntu, make a partition on your Hdd so you can dual boot Ubuntu/Lubuntu. And the answer in my opinion is that you end up with a lot of double apps. So is better to run them separately and that way you will get a true Lubuntu experience. :guitar:

### Post by Borunco on 2012-04-27

It,s recommended to save your files and do a clean install, when upgrading from one release to another. The only exception to that rule in my opinion is, if you already had 12.04 betas or rc installed, then it is just doing sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get install upgrade. and that usually dose it for me. don't get me wrong, I have done upgrade the way you did it, and never had a problem, but things can go wrong.
anyways
enjoy 12.04
borunco

### Post by amjjawad on 2012-04-27
Where is Wubi? there you go:


> That was an intentional change, please read:
 
[https://lists.ubuntu.com/archives/ubuntu-devel/2012-March/034970.html](https://lists.ubuntu.com/archives/ubuntu-devel/2012-March/034970.html)
 
And the bug report requesting the change:
 
[https://bugs.launchpad.net/wubi/+bug/975251](https://bugs.launchpad.net/wubi/+bug/975251)
 
And the first answer here:
 
[http://askubuntu.com/questions/125015/can-i-install-12-04-by-using-wubi](http://askubuntu.com/questions/125015/can-i-install-12-04-by-using-wubi)
 
So Wubi is still available, you simply must just download the wubi.exe (aka: Windows installer) separately:
 
[http://www.ubuntu.com/download/desktop](http://www.ubuntu.com/download/desktop)
 
 
Finally, you can see that here too:

[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PrecisePangolin/ReleaseNotes/Lubuntu#PrecisePangolin.2BAC8-ReleaseNotes.2BAC8-CommonInfrastructure-1.Boot.2C_Installation_and_Post-Installation](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PrecisePangolin/ReleaseNotes/Lubuntu#PrecisePangolin.2BAC8-ReleaseNotes.2BAC8-CommonInfrastructure-1.Boot.2C_Installation_and_Post-Installation)

I'm wondering if it would make a difference [COLOR="Red"]REGARDING LTS SUPPORT,[/COLOR] 

1) to install from the Lubuntu cd

sudo apt-get install lubuntu-desktop

```
and then firefox, evolution, and some other programs I use.

### Post by sudodus on 2012-04-29
> **JC Cheloven said:**
> Hi, this is a question about Lubuntu 12.04 and LTS. Basically I don't undesrtand who maintains what. So:

I'm wondering if it would make a difference [COLOR="Red"]REGARDING LTS SUPPORT,[/COLOR] 

1) to install from the Lubuntu cd 

2) to install a cli system from an alternate Ubuntu CD (regular ubuntu), then ```
sudo apt-get install lubuntu-desktop
```

3) Or alternatively, from the cli system, installing only the basic desktop, for example ```
sudo apt-get install lxde lubuntu-artwork-12-04 lubuntu-artwork lubuntu-default-settings lubuntu-icon-theme
```
and then firefox, evolution, and some other programs I use.

Anyone knows?

I think there is no [easy] way to get Lubuntu LTS. Only the packages that are included in LTS flavours will get LTS support, not packages you add, if they have no such support. So I don't think LXDE or lubuntu-desktop will get any LTS support.

Have a look at the following thread
[[COLOR="Red"]_http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1954702_[/COLOR]]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1954702")

---

### Post by Herpythebrony on 2012-05-04
Fix to any Lubuntu user that has Alsa selecting wrong sound card as default

Go to the terminal and check to see which sound device it picked up

```
alsamixer
```In my case it picked up my usb mic and my eyetoy webcam as default

now to find out the name of the device go to the terminal and type in

```
less /proc/asound/modules
```In my case it was named snd_usb_audio

now become a super user with this command

```
sudo su
```now type in

```
nano /etc/modprobe.d/sound
```It should bring you to a terminal text editor now in this text editor type in

```
options name_of_offending_device index=1
```So in my case it's

```
options snd_usb_audio index=1
```Reboot and it should load the correct sound device!

Herpythebrony~

### Post by bodhi.zazen on 2012-05-14
After much discussion, thread closed.

The forums staff appreciates the dedication and hard work amjjawad has put into the Lubuntu One Stop Thread and recognizes that this thread is an invaluable resource to the Lubuntu community.

However, we now have a thread that has over 500 posts with nuggets of information scattered about it that are impossible to find, and thus does not meet up to [[COLOR="DarkRed"]forums standards for tutorials[/COLOR]](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=677396)

As per [[COLOR="DarkRed"]this thread[/COLOR]](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1949027), we would like to see the information on this thread relocated to the wiki. The advantages of the wiki are that it is Community maintained, peer reviewed, easier to maintain, and easier to find information as compared to a 500 + thread on the forums.

We have staff available to help with convert the information to the wiki, we have asked amjjawad for assistance, and we are also asking the lubuntu community to participate. The wiki is community maintained.

[[COLOR="DarkRed"]bodhi.zazen[/COLOR]](http://ubuntuforums.org/member.php?u=89054) has been working on a script to help convert forums posts -> wiki syntax. [[[COLOR="DarkRed"]link to script on wiki[/COLOR]](http://bodhizazen.net/tweaks/ubforums2ubwiki.sh.txt)].

[[COLOR="DarkOrange"]nothingspecial[/COLOR]](http://ubuntuforums.org/member.php?u=491516) has volunteered from the forums staff to assist the lubuntu community.

See also : [[COLOR="Navy"]Lubuntu Documentation Team[/COLOR]](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Lubuntu/DocumentationTeam)

---

This thread is closed.

The information is now held on the community wiki at [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/LubuntuLinks](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/LubuntuLinks)

Thank you for your thread and the work you have done in keeping it current and of use to the community.

A thread for discussion of the wiki can be found at [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=12062200#post12062200](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=12062200#post12062200)


Support threads regarding the wiki and it's content should be created in a suitable forum.
